<Name>chris mader</Name>< Review>
Good public course with reasonable rates. Beautiful scenery and maintained fairly well. The only downside I would say is that they don’t monitor pace of play. It took us 3.5 hours to play 14 holes. We ended up leaving due to darkness. We paid a twilight rate so that is ok. However, lots of hurry up and wait. If you go, try and go on off hours. It will be worth it.</Review>

Just played last sunday.  the pace was better than i've ever seen but the course was not in great shape.  anywhere around the greens was like hitting off dirt.  the greens were good and the staff is always great but the fairways are terrible and anywhere around the green you might as well putt.  not sure how they can keep charging this prices for a course that gets worse every year.

played again this last sunday 4/11/21 and it is the same.  terrible fairways and hitting out of the sand is like hitting of a sidewalk.  I'd be embarrased to tell people I was the greenskeeper here.</Text>

좋아하는 골프를 일요일 하루밖에 칠수없는 바쁜 우리에게, 평일날 백라인이 있다는건 정말 고마운 코스다. 특히 씨미힐스는 새벽부터 많은 스텝분들이 얼마나 잔듸를 잘 관리하는지 웬만한 프라이빗 골프장과 비교해도 손색이없다.

하지만 한가지... 이렇케 많은분들이 애써서 관리 잘된 골프장을 많은 골퍼들이 첫 대면하는 카운터에서부터 기분이 언짠아 진다면 안될것 같으다.

So here's my story. I've been using the dealership to repair my car for the past two years. Two weeks ago my car starts running really bad, no power, engine pinging and poor gas mileage. I bring my car to the repair department and they call me later that day and tell me my CVT transmission is the problem. It cost $5,000 to replace and I have them do it. A week later I'm driving my car and it starts doing the same exact problems I had the previous week. So I have a friend look at it and it's my air intake hose problem. So I bring my car back to Nissan, I show them the part that is broken and they fix it. Pick my car up and it barely even runs. Turns out because of the air and fuel mixture was wrong. <UserId.>108685370139018629938<//UserId.><Text>Earlier this year, I discovered how much tortillas matter in a taco when I had a "Carnitas Taco" here at Sabor. I was taking my daughter to the nearby Chuck E. Cheese when I realized that I had never eaten a taco in the town of Lemon Grove before, and that this needed to be rectified. Yelp showed Sabor as the highest-rated taqueria in Lemon Grove, but the reviews were mixed among my Yelp friends. I decided to take a chance, and I'm glad I did.

The carnitas in their "Carnitas Taco" were alright. The pieces of pork somewhat resembled the appearance of chopped ham. The meat was flavorful enough and well-seasoned that I went with it, even if I was confused as to what part of the pig I was actually eating. The guacamole was decent and applied with restraint, thankfully. What made this taco special was its magnificent corn tortilla, obviously made on-premises using white masa, with a soft, thick texture and a taste of fresh corn.

Initially, the restaurant was tight-lipped when I probed them about their tortillas, but as I found myself returning for more tacos and other menu items, I got more information. What I can tell you is that Sabor procures their masa from a local supplier in El Cajon that nixtamalizes their own corn in-house, and they believe the key mistake common among tortilla-makers, even professionals, is not using enough water with their masa, resulting in many tortillas being too coarse and dry. And I would say they're right: more moisture results in a heavier, softer, smoother, and more palatable tortilla, as evidenced by the tortillas used with Sabor's tacos.

And, yes, let me be clear: you only get the good tortillas when you order TACOS here. Sabor uses bagged tortillas when served with their non-taco dishes. I suggest anyone who comes here to request their house-made tortillas instead. Better yet, have their fresh tortillas side-by-side with their bagged tortilla and you'll realize how profound of a difference a good corn tortilla makes over the mediocre bagged tortillas.

Sabor's other menu items have been a bit hit-or-miss, which is probably why their Yelp reviews are so mixed -- this is a place where you really need to know what to order. Thankfully, I plan on helping you with that.

The "Bistec Ranchero" is an excellent stew of steak in a spicy tomato sauce with thin strips of crisp onions. Definitely my favorite non-taco item here. The "Torta de Milanesa" is a filling sandwich, and was served on nice toasted bread, though some pieces of beef milanesa were a touch dry. I did not enjoy their "Carne Asada Taco" nearly as much as the Carnitas Taco due to the meat being bland and under-seasoned. Interestingly enough, their "Pollo Asado Plate" is fantastic. I shared it with my daughter, and this was some of the better renditions of pollo asado we've had in San Diego that did not come off my own grill -- the marinade, seasoning, and spices are excellent, and even though the browning is intense, the meat was juicy. Order this instead of the carne asada.

In summary, come to Sabor to experience well-made corn tortillas. Like me, keep coming back for the diversity of their value-oriented menu, of which I plan to continue to work through and appreciate over subsequent visits.<//Text>< Rate>
5<//Rate>

< review>
Stopped in here on a holiday weekend while vacationing across the street.

First of all, the Yelp page shows pizza, which is what we were in the mood for, and why we ended up coming here. THEY DON'T SERVE PIZZA, SO DON'T BE FOOLED LIKE WE WERE.

Beyond that, the service was warm and friendly, but a bit slow, especially given how few customers were in the restaurant. The gnocchi were quite good, and the chicken parm was OK. The singing waitresses is an interesting touch, but it sets this place apart to be sure.

Overall a decent, but not fantastic, experience.< /review>

Visited Comoncy. Food was good, but the help was not.
** Make sure NOT to leave a tip until you leave! (And do so only if you feel a tip is warranted). **
I ordered a triple cappuccino,  but got a regular latte. I told tge waiter, and he said he'd exchange it. Then, he turned around and  started cleaning a table, taking back dirty dishes, etc. When he came back, he started wiping off the dirty table (there were 3 other clean tables, so it's not like that was the only table available! ) I asked if I should take my coffee back to the register, but he said he'd take care of it. Then, continued wiping off that table, the one next to it, arranging the tables and chairs, etc. before finally takung my coffee to be exchanged.  I still onky git a single, not triple shot, but I decided to count my blessings that I got something close to what I ordered.
Then came my order. It looked great, and rasted just as good. However,  the waiter knocked down my knife to the floor when he brought my order. He picjed it up and told mw he'd bring me another one. He dusappeared and didn't see hum until he went to talk to 2 girls who had just sat down. I couldn't get his attention,  I never got my knife,  and not once did he never come by to ask if everything was ok or if we needed anything.
The worst part of this is, when you pay at the register (at the time of your order, of course), you're asked to add your tip amount to your order, BEFORE you have any idea what the service will be like. Also, even though we got some takeout items, and they were labeled as such, they still computed tip on the entire total.
Again, don't tip until the end (and only if you feel a tip is deserved), and make sure it's for the "eat-in" portion only.< /text>

< Text>
I was a former fan of this place. The service was good from Alex. The salad is where it all went downhill. The salad was well constructed, the veggies were good, the blue cheese dressing was tasteless, no discernable bluecheese, the croutons were badly stale. It was my and my wife's anniversary  Then we had the top of the line signature ribeyes. The steaks themselves were on the smallish side. A thick rind of gristle was attached to the fat. The meat wasn't that tender. I'm sorry to see what was a great restaurant fall so far in quality.</Text>
